## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling acceleration (dv/dt) as a function of time and velocity in a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration typically depends on position (which is related to the integral of velocity) and velocity itself, with nonlinear restoring forces and possibly nonlinear damping terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Linear damped oscillator (velocity-dependent)', 'formula': 'dv_dt = c0 * v + c1', 'scenario': 'Simple linear damping or driving, acceleration proportional to velocity'}
- {'name': 'Cubic nonlinear restoring force via velocity proxy', 'formula': 'dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3', 'scenario': 'Duffing-type oscillator where restoring force has cubic nonlinearity'}
- {'name': 'Van der Pol oscillator', 'formula': 'dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)', 'scenario': 'Nonlinear damping with periodic position dependence encoded through time'}
- {'name': 'Sinusoidal restoring force', 'formula': 'dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t + c2)', 'scenario': 'Position is sinusoidal in time for harmonic oscillator, so restoring force is sinusoidal in t'}
- {'name': 'Linear restoring + linear damping', 'formula': 'dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t + c2) + c3 * v', 'scenario': 'Damped harmonic oscillator where position is approximated as sinusoidal'}
- {'name': 'Nonlinear damping with harmonic restoring', 'formula': 'dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t + c2) + c3 * v * (1 - c4 * v**2)', 'scenario': 'Van der Pol type: nonlinear velocity-dependent damping plus sinusoidal restoring force'}
- {'name': 'Quadratic damping', 'formula': 'dv_dt = c0 * v * abs(v) + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)', 'scenario': 'Aerodynamic drag-like damping proportional to v|v| plus restoring force'}
- {'name': 'Polynomial velocity dependence', 'formula': 'dv_dt = c0 + c1 * v + c2 * v**2 + c3 * v**3', 'scenario': 'General polynomial nonlinearity in velocity for nonlinear oscillator'}
- {'name': 'Cosine restoring with velocity damping', 'formula': 'dv_dt = c0 * cos(c1 * t + c2) + c3 * v', 'scenario': 'Harmonic oscillator with position phase-shifted, plus linear damping'}
- {'name': 'Duffing with explicit time-dependent position', 'formula': 'dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * sin(c1 * t)**3 + c3 * v', 'scenario': 'Duffing oscillator with cubic restoring force, position approximated as sinusoidal'}
- {'name': 'Combined harmonic terms', 'formula': 'dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t + c2) + c3 * sin(c4 * t + c5)', 'scenario': 'Superposition of multiple harmonic modes in nonlinear oscillator'}
- {'name': 'Velocity-position coupling via time', 'formula': 'dv_dt = c0 * v * sin(c1 * t + c2)', 'scenario': 'Parametric oscillator or Mathieu-type equation with time-varying coefficient'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring force in oscillators → sinusoidal function of time sin(c*t + c) when position is not directly available but oscillates periodically
- Nonlinear damping in self-excited oscillators → terms like v*(1 - c*v**2) or v**3 representing amplitude-dependent energy exchange
- Phase space reconstruction → when position is unavailable, trigonometric functions of time serve as proxies for position-dependent forces
- Odd-symmetry restoring forces → odd powers of displacement (or velocity in transformed coordinates): v, v**3, v**5
- Frequency doubling/harmonics → presence of sin(2*c*t) or cos(2*c*t) terms indicating nonlinear coupling generating higher harmonics
- Conservative vs dissipative separation → acceleration splits into position-dependent (conservative, via sin/cos of t) and velocity-dependent (dissipative) parts
- Limit cycle behavior → balanced positive and negative damping terms like c0*v + c1*v**3 with opposite signs indicating stable oscillation amplitude

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT: 0.106257*sin(t) - 0.484397*sin(v) - 0.968794*v**

The key components are: `sin(t)`, `sin(v)`, and `v` (linear in v). Let me check each candidate.

### Candidate 1: `c0*sin(t) + v*(c1 + c2*cos(c3*t + c4))`
This gives `c0*sin(t) + c1*v + c2*v*cos(c3*t + c4)`. The GT has no `v*cos(...)` term involving `t`. This term can't be zeroed without losing the `v` dependence structure. We can set c2=0, giving `c0*sin(t) + c1*v`. This misses `sin(v)`.
**Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 2: `c0*sin(t) + v*(c1 + c2*cos(c3*t))`
Same issue as Candidate 1. Setting c2=0 gives `c0*sin(t) + c1*v`, missing `sin(v)`.
**Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 3: `c0*v*Abs(v) + c1*sin(c2 + t) + c3*cos(t) + c4*v + c5*v**3`
Has `sin(c2+t)`, `cos(t)`, `v`, `v*|v|`, `v³`. No `sin(v)`. The `sin(c2+t) + c3*cos(t)` can combine to give `A*sin(t) + B*cos(t)` which is `C*sin(t+φ)`, but we need `sin(v)` which is absent.
**Candidate 3 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 4: `c0*v*Abs(v) + c1*sin(c2 + t) + c3*v + c4*v**3`
No `sin(v)`. Missing basis function.
**Candidate 4 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 5: `c0*sin(t) + c1 + c2*v**2 + c3*log(c4*exp(c5*v) + 1)`
The `log(c4*exp(c5*v) + 1)` is a softplus-like function, not equivalent to `sin(v)`.
**Candidate 5 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 6: `c0*v*Abs(v) + c1*sin(t) + c2*v**3 + c3*v`
No `sin(v)`.
**Candidate 6 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 7: `c0*v**3 + c1*sin(t) + c2*v + v*Abs(v)`
No `sin(v)`.
**Candidate 7 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 8: `c0*sin(t) + c1 + c2*log(c3*exp(c4*v) + 1)`
Softplus, not `sin(v)`.
**Candidate 8 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 9: `c0 + c1*sin(t) + c2*exp(c3*v)`
Exponential in v, not `sin(v)`.
**Candidate 9 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 10: `(c0 + (c1 + c2*sin(t))*(c3*v + c4))/(c3*v + c4)`
Simplify: `c0/(c3*v + c4) + c1 + c2*sin(t)`. This has a `1/(v+const)` term, not `sin(v)` or linear `v`.
**Candidate 10 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 11: `(c0*v + c1 + (c2 + c3*sin(t))*(c4*v + c5))/(c4*v + c5)`
Expand: `(c0*v + c1)/(c4*v + c5) + c2 + c3*sin(t)`. The rational part `(c0*v+c1)/(c4*v+c5)` can be written as `c0/c4 + (c1 - c0*c5/c4)/(c4*v+c5)`. So this is `const + c3*sin(t) + const/(c4*v+c5)`. No `sin(v)` or linear `v`.
**Candidate 11 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 12: `(c0*(c1*v + c2)*sin(t) + c3*v)/(c1*v + c2)`
= `c0*sin(t) + c3*v/(c1*v + c2)`. The second term is `c3*v/(c1*v+c2)` which approaches a constant for large v. Not `sin(v)` or linear `v`.
**Candidate 12 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 13: `c0*sin(t) + c1*log(c2*v + 1)`
Log, not `sin(v)`.
**Candidate 13 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 14: `c0*(c1*v + c2 + c3*(c4 + c5*sin(t)))`
